## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: Solid Mechanics
**Analysis**: This task belongs to Solid Mechanics, as it involves modeling the relationship between stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T). The task is likely related to the study of materials' behavior under different conditions.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Engineering strain: epsilon = (L_f - L_i) / L_i (relationship between strain and material deformation)
- Stress-strain curve: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon (Hooke's law)
- Thermal expansion: epsilon = c0 * (T - T0) (linear expansion of a material with temperature change)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon^2 (nonlinear elastic deformation)
- Viscoelastic model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon^c2 (time-dependent deformation)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: E(T) = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (change in elastic modulus with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent yield stress: sigma_y(T) = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (change in yield stress with temperature)
- Material damping: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon^c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (dissipation of energy in materials)
- Creep model: epsilon = c0 * t**c1 * sigma**c2 (time-dependent deformation under constant stress)
- Cyclic deformation model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon^c2 + c3 * t (fatigue behavior under cyclic loading)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Ratcheting damage accumulation → Piecewise functions, cumulative summation
- Creep/relaxation → Exponential decay envelope, power-law relaxation
- Hardening/softening → Rational fraction, selective Abs, peak function
- Fracture/damage → Logarithmic distribution, crack propagation model
- Material coupling → Variable products, cross-coupling between different physical quantities
- Damping/energy dissipation → Exponential decay envelope, power-law dissipation
- Nonlinear elasticity → Polynomial terms of order higher than 2
- Time-dependent deformation → Exponential decay envelope, power-law relaxation

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.5449782742323234*(T - 352.1579043725849) + epsilon**0.6261602091724962*1.5180288401497986*(T - 352.1579043725849)`

Let me expand this:
GT = -0.5450*(T - 352.16) + 1.5180*epsilon^0.6262*(T - 352.16)
GT = -0.5450*T + 191.92 + 1.5180*T*epsilon^0.6262 - 534.58*epsilon^0.6262

So GT has the form: **a*T + b*T*epsilon^c + d*epsilon^c + e**

where:
- a = -0.5450 (coefficient of T)
- b = 1.5180 (coefficient of T*epsilon^c)
- c = 0.6262 (exponent)
- d = -534.58 (coefficient of epsilon^c)
- e = 191.92 (constant)

The basis functions are: {T, T*epsilon^c, epsilon^c, 1}
